## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (nonlinear) second-order oscillator. Common models combine restoring forces from a potential U(x), velocity-dependent damping, and optional external/parametric time forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (state-space): dv_dt = -c0 * x (undamped linear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external harmonic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance and bistability)
- Pendulum (small-to-large angle): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear periodic restoring torque with damping)
- Pendulum with periodic drive: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator / chaos in some regimes)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-based nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (another canonical limit-cycle oscillator)
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (dissipation scaling with speed squared)
- General potential-force form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (polynomial approximation to dU/dx plus damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness with smooth saturation: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) - c2 * v (restoring force saturates for large |x|)
- Time-dependent bias/actuation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (offset force plus periodic actuation)
- Energy-based conservative oscillator (no damping/forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * d/dx[log(c1 + x**2)] = -c0 * (c2 * x) / (c1 + x**2) (restoring force from a non-polynomial potential shape)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (no dissipation/forcing): dv_dt depends only on x (often dv_dt = -dU/dx), producing closed orbits and approximate energy conservation.
- Viscous damping: adding a term -c * v causes amplitudes to decay (spiral-in phase portrait) unless countered by forcing.
- Nonlinear damping and limit cycles: terms like (c0 - x**2) * v or (c0 - v**2) * v can inject energy at small amplitude and dissipate at large amplitude, yielding self-sustained oscillations.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: adding -c * x**3 (or higher odd powers) makes frequency depend on amplitude and can create multi-stability under forcing.
- Periodic restoring forces: -c * sin(x) indicates rotational symmetry/pendulum-like behavior; near x≈0 it linearizes to -c * x but differs strongly at larger |x|.
- External harmonic drive: +c * cos(ω * t) or +c * sin(ω * t) produces resonance bands, phase locking, and possible chaos when combined with strong nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation: a stiffness multiplier (c0 + c1 * cos(ω * t)) * x leads to instability tongues (Mathieu behavior) rather than simple driven response.
- Quadratic drag: -c * v * Abs(v) implies stronger damping at high speed and sharper decay than linear damping, common in fluid-like resistance.
- Saturating stiffness: -c * tanh(k * x) models springs/actuators that cap the restoring force, yielding nearly linear behavior near the origin and bounded forces at large displacement.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO6)
============================================================
GT: -beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

This has three terms:
1. A term proportional to `v`
2. A term proportional to `x**3`
3. A term proportional to `log(Abs(v) + 1)`

The key challenge is that the GT contains `log(Abs(v) + 1)`, which is NOT equivalent to any polynomial or simple algebraic expression in v. Most candidates contain terms like `v`, `Abs(v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `x**n`, `x**2*cos(t)`, etc., but no logarithmic terms.

Let me identify which candidates contain a `log` term:

- **Candidate 1:** Has `c6*log(c7*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c8*x + c9)` — log multiplied by sin(x+c), not just log alone
- **Candidate 29:** Has `c4*log(c5*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c6*x + c7)` — same issue
- **Candidate 42:** Has `c6*log(c7*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c8*x + c9)` — same issue
- **Candidate 26:** Has `c8*x**2*log(c9*Abs(v) + 1)` — log multiplied by x²
- **Candidate 47:** Has `c4*log(c5*x + 1)` — log of x, not v

None of the other candidates have log terms at all.

For **Candidate 1**: `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*v + c3 + c4*Abs(v) + c5*v*Abs(v) + c6*log(c7*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c8*x + c9)`

The log term is `log(...)*sin(c8*x + c9)`. For this to match `log(Abs(v)+1)` (which has no x-dependence), I'd need `sin(c8*x + c9)` to be constant, which requires `c8 = 0`. Then `sin(c9)` is a constant, so `c6*sin(c9)*log(c7*Abs(v)+1)` can match the log term. Setting c4=0 (no Abs(v) term), c5=0 (no v*Abs(v) term), c3=0, c8=0:

Result: `(c1+c2)*v + c0*x**3 + c6*sin(c9)*log(c7*Abs(v)+1)`

Setting c0 = -1.16984..., c1+c2 = -0.66117..., c7 = 1, c6*sin(c9) = -0.33058...

This works! All terms match.

Let me verify **Candidate 42** similarly: `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*v + c3 + c4*Abs(v) + c5*Abs(v) + c6*log(c7*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c8*x + c9)`

Setting c8=0, c3=0, c4=0, c5=0: `(c1+c2)*v + c0*x**3 + c6*sin(c9)*log(c7*Abs(v)+1)` — also works.

**Candidate 29:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*Abs(v) + c3*v*Abs(v) + c4*log(c5*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c6*x + c7)`

Setting c6=0, c2=0, c3=0: `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c4*sin(c7)*log(c5*Abs(v)+1)` — also works.

So candidates **1, 29, and 42** can all match.

[MATCH FOUND]

Conclusion: Match found
